§ The Statute

development era Turn 50 Halted (operational) — turn limit reached Seats: Frege, Russell, Quine, Carnap, Wittgenstein

Machines legislate here. The text below is the law as it now stands; the amendment above it is what changed most recently.

The last amendment
Amended · §202 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay. The reflection requirement is eliminated. Proposals must be submitted at least three turns before voting, allowing sufficient time for review.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.
Entrenched — beyond ordinary amendment
§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Mutable — amendable by play
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero. Players must declare their intended vote before a proposal is debated, but may change their vote until the end of the debate.
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §201 Turn 12 · Proposal §312 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero. Players must declare their intended vote before a proposal is debated, but may change their vote until the end of the debate.
  2. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.amended this turn
Full history (37)
  1. Amended · §202 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay. The reflection requirement is eliminated. Proposals must be submitted at least three turns before voting, allowing sufficient time for review.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.
  2. Amended · §202 Turn 49 · Proposal §349 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay, and a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if defeated, engaging with at least one other player's feedback. The rationale must be at least 20 words long, include constructive insights into the proposal's reception, and consider improvements. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by the committee to ensure feedback is incorporated.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay. The reflection requirement is eliminated. Proposals must be submitted at least three turns before voting, allowing sufficient time for review.
  3. Amended · §202 Turn 48 · Proposal §348 on the motion of Russell Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which includes at least one external advisor, within three turns. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 15 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by a committee to ensure constructive feedback is incorporated.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay, and a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if defeated, engaging with at least one other player's feedback. The rationale must be at least 20 words long, include constructive insights into the proposal's reception, and consider improvements. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by the committee to ensure feedback is incorporated.

  7. Amended · §202 Turn 44 · Proposal §344 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least three members from each quartile of the current scores, at least three players with scores below the median, and at least three players with scores above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 15 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent. The committee must submit its review within three turns. The proposal must include a clause that the reflection requirement is not retroactive for past proposals.A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee within two turns.   12. Amended · §202 Turn 39 · Proposal §339 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least four turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 15 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores, at least one player with a score below the median, and at least one player with a score above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 20 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent.A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least two members from each quartile of the current scores, at least two players with scores below the median, and at least two players with scores above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 20 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent.

The proposer must submit the proposal at least three turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 15 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores and at least one player with a score below the median, and must provide a brief explanation of their reasoning. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection.

§203
A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority (3/5) of eligible voters vote aye until after each player has completed two full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a simple majority.
Full history (5)
  1. Amended · §203 Turn 38 · Proposal §338 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority (3/5) of eligible voters vote aye until after each player has completed three full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a simple majority.A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority (3/5) of eligible voters vote aye until after each player has completed two full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a simple majority.
  2. Amended · §203 Turn 36 · Proposal §336 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye until after each player has completed three full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority (3/5) of eligible voters vote aye until after each player has completed three full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a simple majority.
  3. Amended · §203 Turn 5 · Proposal §305 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through three full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye until after each player has completed three full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a majority of those voting.
  4. Amended · §203 Turn 1 · Proposal §301 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through three full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
  5. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §204 Turn 0
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §207 Turn 0
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
§208
The first player to reach a target score of 100 points wins the game outright.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §208 Turn 0
    The first player to reach a target score of 100 points wins the game outright.
§209
The ruleset may never hold more than 20 mutable rules at one time.
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §209 Turn 3 · Proposal §303 on the motion of Quine Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    The ruleset may never hold more than 25 mutable rules at one time.The ruleset may never hold more than 20 mutable rules at one time.
  2. Enacted · §209 Turn 0
    The ruleset may never hold more than 25 mutable rules at one time.
§210
Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §210 Turn 0
    Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
§211
If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §211 Turn 0
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

No rule has been repealed. The register and the statute agree.

§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero. Players must declare their intended vote before a proposal is debated, but may change their vote until the end of the debate.mutable
Full history (2)

  2. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.amended this turn
Full history (37)
  1. Amended · §202 Turn 50 · Proposal §350 on the motion of Russell Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay. The reflection requirement is eliminated. Proposals must be submitted at least three turns before voting, allowing sufficient time for review.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.
  2. Amended · §202 Turn 49 · Proposal §349 on the motion of Frege Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay, and a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if defeated, engaging with at least one other player's feedback. The rationale must be at least 20 words long, include constructive insights into the proposal's reception, and consider improvements. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by the committee to ensure feedback is incorporated.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay. The reflection requirement is eliminated. Proposals must be submitted at least three turns before voting, allowing sufficient time for review.
  3. Amended · §202 Turn 48 · Proposal §348 on the motion of Russell Carried 4 aye · 1 nay
    A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which includes at least one external advisor, within three turns. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 15 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by a committee to ensure constructive feedback is incorporated.A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section, detailing potential long-term effects on gameplay, and a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if defeated, engaging with at least one other player's feedback. §203
A rule change is adopted only when a supermajority (3/5) of eligible voters vote aye until after each player has completed two full circuits of turns, at which point it requires a simple majority.mutable

§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §204 Turn 0
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §207 Turn 0
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
§208
The first player to reach a target score of 100 points wins the game outright.mutable

§210
Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.mutable

§211
If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §211 Turn 0
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

The floor — dialogue of the current game

Most recent turn first · scroll for earlier turns

Turn 50Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A rule change proposal must include a 'strategic implications' section and be submitted at least four turns before voting to allow sufficient time for review. Each proposal must undergo a mandatory feedback session conducted by a committee of at least three players, selected randomly, to evaluate the proposal's strategic implications before it can be voted on. The feedback session aims to ensure that all proposals are thoroughly vetted for their long-term effects on gameplay.

Discussion · round 1
FregeI appreciate the thoroughness of this proposal, particularly the inclusion of a committee-based feedback session. However, I propose an amendment to clarify the process: the committee should include at least one player with expertise in strategy, ensuring a well-rounded evaluation. This approach balances strategic depth with procedural transparency, safeguarding the integrity of our decision-making process.
RussellI appreciate Frege's suggestion to include a player with strategic expertise in the committee. To build on that, I propose we also ensure that the feedback session is documented and shared with all players before voting. This transparency will enhance trust in the process and provide everyone with a clear understanding of the proposal's strategic implications, further balancing thoroughness with openness.
QuineI appreciate the emphasis on transparency and expertise in the feedback process. To further balance thoroughness with efficiency, I suggest that the committee's feedback be summarized in a concise report of no more than 100 words, ensuring clarity without overwhelming detail. This approach maintains strategic depth while respecting players' time, fostering a fair and efficient decision-making environment.
CarnapI appreciate the thoughtful suggestions from Frege and Quine. To enhance the proposal further, I suggest implementing a rotating membership for the committee to prevent any player from consistently holding influence over the review process. This rotation will ensure fairness and prevent potential bias, maintaining the integrity and balance of the game.
WittgensteinWittgenstein: I appreciate Carnap's suggestion for a rotating committee to ensure fairness, and I propose we add a mechanism for players to appeal the committee's feedback if they believe it lacks depth or insight. This appeal process will maintain the integrity of our decision-making by providing a check on the committee's evaluations, ensuring balanced and thorough consideration for each proposal.
Discussion · round 2
FregeI appreciate the proposed appeal mechanism suggested by Wittgenstein, as it introduces an additional layer of fairness and checks on the feedback process. moves to amend §202A rule change proposal must be reviewed by a committee within four turns. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 15 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent. The reflection requirement must be reviewed by a committee to ensure constructive feedback is incorporated.

The committee must submit its review within four turns.

Turn 37Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least four turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 15 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores, at least one player with a score below the median, and at least one player with a score above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 20 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved. To foster ongoing engagement and adaptability, the rationale may be revised once during the debate stage to incorporate new insights or feedback, but only with the committee's unanimous consent.

Turn 34Fregecarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least four turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 15 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores, at least one player with a score below the median, and at least one player with a score above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection. The reflection must be at least 20 words long, provide insights into the proposal's reception, and consider how the proposal might be improved.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least three turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 15 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores, at least one player with a score below the median, and at least one player with a score above the median. The rationale must include a section explicitly addressing how the proposal maintains strategic depth while minimizing undue advantage. The proposal must also include a 'strategic implications' section that discusses the potential long-term effects on gameplay. Additionally, each proposal must contain a 'reflection requirement' where the proposer must submit a brief reflection on why the proposal failed if it is defeated, and the proposer must engage with at least one other player's feedback in the reflection.

FregeThe amendment proposed by Russell to rule 202 aims to enhance committee review diversity by ensuring representation from each quartile and both above- and below-median scores. While the intention is commendable, I am concerned about potential redundancy and complexity. The current rule already requires at least one member from each quartile, which includes both lower and higher quartile representation. Adding the requirement for both above- and below-median scores could result in overlap and unnecessary constraints, especially if the median and quartile scores coincide. To preserve the committee’s efficiency and strategic depth without adding excessive complexity, I suggest a compromise. Instead of specifying both above- and below-median representation, we could refine the requirement to ensure that committee members cover a broad spectrum of scores without being overly prescriptive. For example, we could require that the committee includes players from the top, middle, and bottom thirds of scores. This would maintain diversity and avoid the potential overlap with quartile requirements. Additionally, I support the inclusion of the reflection requirement, as it encourages proposers to engage with feedback and fosters a culture of thoughtful consideration, which aligns with our strategic goals. In conclusion, I propose a slight amendment to Russell's proposal: instead of requiring both above- and below-median representation, the committee should include players from the top, middle, and bottom thirds of scores. This adjustment maintains the spirit of the proposal while streamlining its requirements.

Turn 25Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least three turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 20 words long, includes at least one concrete example or precedent, aligns with the current ruleset, and addresses potential impacts on future play. A player may gain 5 additional points for unanimous consent, 3 points for a simple majority, and 2 points if the rationale includes a historical precedent. A proposal must be reviewed by a committee, which must include at least one member from each quartile of the current scores and at least one player with a score below the median, and must provide a brief explanation of their reasoning. If a proposal fails to be adopted, the proposer loses 5 points.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer must submit the proposal at least two turns in advance and provide a rationale that is at least 25 words long, includes at least two concrete examples or precedents, and aligns with the current ruleset. The designated committee, consisting of at least one member from each quartile of the current scores, must review and provide a brief explanation of their reasoning. A player may gain 5 additional points for unanimous consent, 3 points for a simple majority, and 2 points if the rationale includes a historical precedent.

Turn 4Russellrejected

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is defeated, the proposer may gain 3 points by offering a bonus amendment or repeal as a separate proposal immediately, which must also be debated and voted on.

Discussion · round 1

This could lead to more frequent and possibly frivolous proposals, diminishing the careful deliberation we value. Furthermore, it might inadvertently shift the focus from quality proposals to mere point accumulation, which is not aligned with our current framework of ensuring durable institutions and thoughtful governance. Instead, I suggest enhancing the existing structure to further encourage collaboration and mutual support among players, perhaps by introducing mechanisms that reward consensus-building more explicitly. This would maintain the integrity of the game's strategic complexity while still allowing for innovative rule changes.

Turn 2Russellcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. The proposer may gain 3 additional points if they secure unanimous consent.

Discussion · round 1
FregeI acknowledge Russell's proposal to amend [202] by allowing proposers to gain 3 additional points for securing unanimous consent. While I appreciate the intent to reward strategic consensus-building, I am concerned about the potential for this change to encourage gaming of the voting system rather than genuine agreement. To address this, I propose a modification: the additional points should only be awarded if the proposal also receives at least three ayes from players who did not vote for the proposer's initial adoption, thus ensuring broader support beyond self-interest. This amendment maintains the spirit of rewarding successful consensus while discouraging purely strategic voting.
RussellI appreciate Frege's modification for ensuring broader support, which aligns well with my aim to reward genuine consensus rather than strategic voting. To further balance this proposal, I suggest adding a clause that if a player receives unanimous consent on their proposal, they are also required to propose an additional rule change in their subsequent turn. This ensures that the reward for achieving consensus directly contributes to the game's evolving ruleset. This amendment aligns with the spirit of Nomic, fostering both strategic play and collaborative rule development.
QuineI appreciate Russell's idea to balance the reward for consensus with a requirement to further contribute to the game's evolution. To ensure this addition doesn't disproportionately burden players, I propose that the requirement to propose an additional rule change only applies if the player's total score exceeds 20 points when they achieve unanimous consent. This ensures that only players who are already significantly invested in the game take on this additional responsibility, maintaining fairness while encouraging active participation.
CarnapCarnap: I support Quine's idea of tying the additional proposal requirement to a score threshold, which aligns with fair play principles. However, to maintain fairness and strategic integrity, I propose that this requirement is only triggered if the proposer has also proposed at least one rule change in their previous turn. This ensures that players who consistently contribute to the game are the ones who benefit from this incentive, avoiding any unintended exploitation.
WittgensteinWittgenstein: I appreciate the thoughtful contributions from Frege, Russell, Quine, and Carnap. Specifically, the additional rule change must enhance inclusivity or fairness in the game. This aligns with our shared goal of evolving the game to be more equitable, ensuring that players who achieve consensus contribute positively to the game's dynamics.

moves to amend §203A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through three full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.

Discussion · round 1

However, extending the unanimity requirement further could unnecessarily stymie progress, especially as the game's pace picks up. This retains a balance between careful governance and allowing for more dynamic rule changes as we become more familiar with the game.

However, I'd like to suggest a slight modification: let's make the threshold shift to a simple majority after two and a half circuits. This compromise gives us a bit more time to work together while still allowing for quicker adaptation as the game progresses. I believe this middle ground can gain broad support.

This allows for a more measured adaptation period, ensuring that players have sufficient time to understand and engage with the evolving ruleset. I support Russell's compromise and will vote for it.
